My top 3 choices are: the Tom Kah soup, Pad Thai and Pad See Ew, but the papaya salad is slowly about to take over one of those spots! With the days getting hotter and hotter I find their papaya salad really hits the spot. (I usually order a side of sticky rice with my papaya salad.) I like it on the spicy side so I ask for "medium" on their mild-medium-hot scale. The Thai tea is okay, but sometimes it really is over or under the right amount of sweetness.
Parking lot is nearly impossible now! Plan to circle the lot many times... And then park on the street. Maybe, if your lucky enough to find one!</Text>

<Review>This outstanding establishment is unique in many ways. Great owners, Robbie and Tom Nelson,  and support staff.    Audrey, Dianne, Kimber, and my great friend, Dale. No better people in this world than them.
Robbie's kitchen is like no other in Cali. Everything that she serves is outstanding , freshest ingredients, plus everything is homemade with her heart. Plenty of cold beer and an array of wines and specialty libations, however for your info, no hard liquor is served.
For me personally, they offer 2 pool tournaments each and every week
8ball on Wed nite and 9ball on Sunday nights, but must be signed up by 6:55 each evening. No exceptions, 7:05 too late. Competitive, but loads of fun.
Finally, I love this place for the people, especially the locals, who walk thru there front door.
Lastly, on Sat night,  they have some of the best Karaoke singers in Mariposa county and surrounding areas. They fire this up usually around 8:00 pm and shut it down around midnight.
All in all, the Airport Inn, is your best bet to enjoy a magnificent experience,  so come and mix it up with my friends and myself.
Make it a point to stop in and say hello to Tom and Robbie, and the gang.

<name>Garry Corret< /name><Review>If you've read or seen the film 'The Prestige', you'll be a fan of this slightly hidden from sight cocktail bar located in the newly renovated Robertson Plaza.

The cocktail menu is separated into the three parts of a magic trick - The Pledge, The Turn, and The Prestige. The Pledge focuses on the seemingly normal with slight variation made to the classics. The Turn transforms the seemingly normal to the extraordinary by turning the twist up a notch. The Prestige is the culminating final act that combines the lessons of the first two acts and spins up something even more grandeur; cocktails on this page focus on layering unique ingredients together to create a complex palette.

Behind the scenes, all the best practices of composing a standard craft cocktail follow. This includes the chilled glassware, the chipping away of large chunks of clear ice, and the right aromatic toppings.

The interior is beautifully decorated and follows an art deco look. Beautiful lighting decorate the cabinet fixtures and ceiling.

I had the Sing Sing from the Prestige page, which based on the name & ingredients seemed to be an evolution of the Singapore Sling. Unlike the usual sweetness of the Sling, the Sing balanced the taste and packed quite a punch. It was a refreshing kick to start the evening.<//Review>< gmapID>

< Review>
Bibo is hands down my favorite cocktail bar in this part of town! Yes, beauty is in the eye of the beholder, but I really dig the ambiance and the art deco decor. The entrance is semi-hidden, tucked away in the corner of a plaza. Can't speak too much about the food, but I would recommend nearly every drink I've had here. The drink menu is really quite creative the way the drinks are organized. Staff is knowledgable as well and can give great recommendations if you're unsure of what to order.

Note that they also have a stellar happy hour weekdays from 5-7pm with $6 martinis and $8 wines. When they first opened a bit over a year ago it was never too crowded, but it seems like more and more people have been stopping by as of late. I guess the secret is out!<//Review>

<user_id>114706465257781422918< /user_id><resp>None< /resp>< Text>
My sister and I have been to Blue Moon twice. Both times were for lunch. We are not Asian but everyone else in the full restaurant was. Blue Moon offers a nice lunch menu with each item $6.45 (with tax, = $7.00!) My sister ordered a fish dish over rice and a delicious sauce. General serving - she ate every bite. I had the sesame chicken with rice. Everything was steaming hot and fresh. We spoke with a couple of other diners and they explained what they were eating. We almost got whiplash twisting our heads to see what was coming out of the kitchen next. Oh, drinks came with the lunch specials. I must admit, no refills were included.

If you like karaoke, this might be an interesting place. It is not a night club environment. Rooms of various sizes designed to accommodate small to large groups are located in the rear of the restaurant. Each room has seating and TV. For a fee, you gather your group and make your own private karaoke party.

I go for the food. Most of it is Hong Kong Style. We had no problem with the service. She was attentive and prompt. I like it! Thumbs up.< /Text>

< Review>
We have not been here for several months and decided to drop in today.  Our previous experiences with the food  were not good after the original owner sold the restaurant. However today seemed to be much better. We ordered hot and sour soup to share. Its a large bowl big enough for several cups each and loaded with stuff. I don't care for the flavor of bamboo and unfortunately it was loaded with bamboo. Next time I will advise them to leave it out. But it was spicy and flavorful. We also ordered eggplant with pork in a hot pot over rice. So very yummy. I was sorry I didn't take another order to go for dinner!üê∑
We finished with a scoop of Mango icecreme.  Creamy fruity flavor to complete a nice meal. Be aware the ice cream is now 2.50 a scoop not 1.75 as stated on the menu.  Guess the staff didn't even know the price was wrong on the menu. The waitress was nice but very hard to understand unless you speak Chinese and we don't.  In spite of that we all managed ok.  We will be going back soon and I will be willing to try some of the dishes we used to enjoy here again. We like to support local businesses.  Give them a try!< /Review>

<review>Been here twice and i'm always more than satisfied! :)
We always go during happy hour though, it's a lot more affordable per hour.
I especially love that their karaoke rooms are private so you don't have to humiliate yourself in front of strangers, you can just humiliate yourself in the comfort of your friends.
I've only ordered their fried rice and broccoli beef and its pretty good, not the best, but it's not bad either.
The place is always clean, and they always offer brand new(sealed) covers for the mics- for those of you who find it necessary to sing with the mic pressed up against your lips (gross!)
in the end we (my friends and i) always split the bill accordingly, and the lady that works there is always nice enough to go through the trouble of calculating it all and charging it all separate for us, even though i can tell it's a BIG hassle for her.
This place is a definite check out/hangout place, why are you still reading this?! GO! :)<//review>< Pics>

<rate>4< /rate>< review>
Let me start off by saying that I have NEVER felt compelled enough to actually share anything negative about business, until today! I have been to L.B Market Nails & Spa dozens of times on my own and have had very pleasant experiences. That is why I was astounded by the way I was treated when I went in with my disabled sister yesterday. We did not receive the usual greeting or hello. After standing there for a while (being stared at like we were aliens), I told them we had appointments at 5pm. They looked at me and said ‚ÄúOh, just for you, right?‚Äù I said no, that we both had appointments. They acted like they had never seen a lady in a wheelchair before in their life! I said she needed pedicure and I needed an SNS manicure. The manager, Lua, walked over and immediately created a scene rudely saying that she didn‚Äôt think my sister would be able to get into the spa chair. I politely told her that their pedicure chairs are the same as every other salon we have been to and that it was not a problem. (See photo below at another salon) My sister has been getting pedicures biweekly for years and she sits perfectly fine in them. I then transferred her from her wheelchair into the spa chair with ease as we have always done. Lua stood there and kept arguing that my sister is not safe in their chair. Again, I explained to her that my sister is completely safe. I explained that her disability does not affect her brain. I educated her that cerebral palsy affects her body only and she is not going to throw herself out of the chair. I reassured her that she can understand everything we are saying even though she can not verbalize it. Lua said I would need to sit next to her the whole time because they didn‚Äôt have a seatbelt. I said she didn‚Äôt need a seatbelt because it‚Äôs not a moving wheelchair but I had no problem sitting next to her while she got her pedicure and I got my nails done in the seat next to her. Lua said I would need to wait until her pedicure was over before I could get my nails done because she was not safe. I told her that was ridiculous. We should be able to have our services at the same time as we always do. I told her we would be late for our dinner plans if we had to do one of us at a time. That is why we made appointments for both of us at 5.  At this point, Lua had made us feel embarrassed and totally unwelcome. I explained that we did not appreciate the harassment or discrimination. I asked Lua if she knew anything about ADA. She said she did but I argued that if that were true then she would not be so blatantly disrespectIng our rights. It is my sister‚Äôs right to determine if she feels safe, not Lua‚Äôs. She refused to have our services done concurrently even if I sat in a chair beside her. I explained over and over how many different salons we have been to over the years (my sis is 46 and I‚Äôm 40) and how we have never had a problem or been treated so poorly but she would not budge. This treatment went on for over 10 minutes despite the fact that my sister had been sitting comfortably in their chair the whole time. I looked around and one young woman customer quietly shrugged and mouthed ‚ÄòI‚Äôm sorry‚Äô. We ended up leaving in tears for the embarrassment my sister had endured. I NEVER want another disabled person to be treated the way we were in this salon ever again. Being a flight attendant and in the service industry myself I‚Äôm appalled that something like this is happening in 2020. Flight attendants are great about spreading the word and I personally know hundreds of colleagues in the area. I‚Äôm going to tell our story and then have them share our story. I 100% believe in boycotting. We are friends with business owners in Long Beach and I‚Äôm sure they are going to want to know what‚Äôs going on in their community so they can help end this kind of injustice! Long Beach, Calif.< /review>

After searching for a dentist for months I finally went to Bancroft Dental Care. Great service and great staff, but unfortunately what seemed to be great hours are not and sadly I found this out after my visit when they recommended a deep cleaning, I agreed and tried to schedule an appointment, but it turns out they only provide that type of service between 9 a.m. - 3 p.m. M-F.
